  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_43685424-4963-4271-8bce-520035d6599b'

  <span id="freeText6955080615224829125" style="display:none"><b>In which a humble young carpet merchant wins, then loses, the princess of his dreams</b><br /><br />Far to the south of the land of Ingary, in the Sultanates of Rashpuht, there lived in the city of Zanzib a young and not very prosperous carpet dealer named Abdullah who loved to spend his time daydreaming. He was content with his life and his daydreams until, one day, a stranger sold him a magic carpet.<br /><br />That very night, the carpet flew him to an enchanted garden. There, he met and fell in love with the beauteous princess Flower-in-the-Night, only to have her snatched away, right under his very nose, by a wicked djinn. With only his magic carpet and his wits to help him, Abdullah sets off to rescue his princess....</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">They are in this, but one of them doesn't show up until the middle of the story, the other until nearly the end. However, if you're paying attention, <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">They are in this, but one of them doesn't show up until the middle of the story, the other until nearly the end. However, if you're paying attention, you can actually figure out where they are much sooner than that.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1303555588" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17871554189319508071">Another very readable book from DWJ, and one I've just finished reading to my daughter, Celyn. Refreshingly independent princesses being semi-saved by our devoted hero, a carpet salesman from the desert city of Zanzib. He's not hero material, and never resorts to violence, but he's a good fellow and carries the story well.<br/><br/>We get all the standard Aladdin-esque trappings, a magic carpet, a genie in a bottle, evil djinns, bandits, sultans, camels... and for a while you think you know roughly where </span>
  <span id="freeText17871554189319508071" style="display:none">Another very readable book from DWJ, and one I've just finished reading to my daughter, Celyn. Refreshingly independent princesses being semi-saved by our devoted hero, a carpet salesman from the desert city of Zanzib. He's not hero material, and never resorts to violence, but he's a good fellow and carries the story well.<br /><br />We get all the standard Aladdin-esque trappings, a magic carpet, a genie in a bottle, evil djinns, bandits, sultans, camels... and for a while you think you know roughly where it's all heading. Then things veer northwards and we find ourselves treading old ground. Greener ground. Zeroing in on territory thoroughly trodden in book 1. You'll find yourself anticipating the reappearance of the Wizard Howl and Sophie.<br /><br />The ending was where things fell apart a little for me, and perhaps for Celyn judging by the somewhat bemused silence she greeted it with (she's non-verbal but normally makes her views known). In a frantic rush everything seems to turn into everything else - like the Scooby Doo mask-pulling finale ... on speed.<br /><br />Anyhow, it was good at the end to finally catch up with Sophie and Howl. We're moving onto the third book of the trilogy next - looking forward to it.<br /><br /><br /> <a href="http://eepurl.com/cimnK1" rel="nofollow noopener">Join my 3-emails-a-year newsletter #prizes</a><br /><br />...</span>

<div id="review_15591188" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15591188" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75857-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556514715p2/75857.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15591188?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/75857-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15591188" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13213967003546932204">"Castle in the Air" is Diana Wynne Jones' sequel to her amazingly awesome novel "Howl's Moving Castle." It was originally published in 1990 (four years after "Howl's Moving Castle"). At first glance, this novel doesn't sound like a sequel--it sounds more like a companion book at best--but I promise it does explain more about Howl and Sophie, just not right away and not, perhaps, in the most obvious way.<br/><br/>That said, this story is set in the Sultanates of Rashpuht a land far to the south of Ingary (</span>
  <span id="freeText13213967003546932204" style="display:none">"Castle in the Air" is Diana Wynne Jones' sequel to her amazingly awesome novel "Howl's Moving Castle." It was originally published in 1990 (four years after "Howl's Moving Castle"). At first glance, this novel doesn't sound like a sequel--it sounds more like a companion book at best--but I promise it does explain more about Howl and Sophie, just not right away and not, perhaps, in the most obvious way.<br /><br />That said, this story is set in the Sultanates of Rashpuht a land far to the south of Ingary (where Howl and Sophie make their home). Instead of a land akin to King Arthur and Merlin, Rashpuht is much more likely to harbor Aladdin and other desert-dwellers. This change in setting, along with a new protagonist, make for the most dramatic differences between "Castle in the Air" and its predecessor.<br /><br />Abdullah works as a carpet merchant in the city of Zanzib. Abdullah's stall may not be as prosperous as his father's first wife's relatives would like, but Abdullah can't stand most of them so he doesn't worry too much. What really bothers Abdullah is the fact that he's selling carpets at all. Abdullah is convinced there is more to life and spends a good deal of his time daydreaming about what his life could be like if, say, he were a prince who had escaped bandits and disguised himself as a carpet merchant before he found his true love.<br /><br />All in all, the young man doesn't give his daydreams much thought until he is sold a mysterious carpet. With the carpet, Abdullah finds that all of his dreams seem to be coming true with alarming accuracy. Whisked to a magical garden, Abdullah meets and falls in love with the beautiful and intelligent Flower-in-the-Night only to have her abducted by an evil djinn. So begins Abdullah's adventure as he and his carpet set off to rescue his true love.<br /><br />This being a novel by Diana Wynne Jones, the plot is filled with charming twists and enjoyable characters throughout. The other great thing about this novel is how much Jones fleshes out the world she introduced in "Howl's Moving Castle." As the novel progresses, readers learn more about the relations between Ingary, Rashpuht, and Strangia (a land that becomes important later, trust me). At the same time, Jones also creates a completely new set of customs and even a new diction for her Rashpuhtian characters which gives the novel an impressive depth.<br /><br />I don't know if this was the intended effect but, even though both novels are written in English, this change in diction also creates the effect that the characters here speak a different language and that, on some level, their customs would be very foreign to those found in Ingary. One of Jones' best inventions is that buyers and sellers in Zanzib always speak to each other "in the most formal and flowery way." This habit creates a lot of conversations that function on a variety of levels much in the same way body language can add to an exchange. For example:<br /><br /> "It is possible that my low and squalid establishment might provide that which you seek, O pearl of wanderers," he said, and cast his eye critically over the stranger's dirty desert robe, the corroded stud in the side of the man's nose, and his tattered headcloth as he said it.<br /><br /> "It is worse than squalid, mighty seller of floor coverings," the stranger agreed.<br /><br />Exchanges like this appear throughout the novel and make it really enjoyable to read. At the same time this type of double talk suggests that Abdullah is a shrewder narrator than Sophie might have been at the start of the novel. Abdullah doesn't always know exactly what's going on during the novel, but he always tries to make sure he comes out on top (or at least not on a forty foot pole).<br /><br />On its own, "Castle in the Air" is a lot of fun as far as fantasies go. Read in combination with "<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294.Howl_s_Moving_Castle__Howl_s_Moving_Castle___1_" title="Howl's Moving Castle (Howl's Moving Castle, #1) by Diana Wynne Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">Howl's Moving Castle</a>" and "House of Many Ways" (Jones' latest novel featuring Howl and Sophie due out in June 2008) this book is excellent.<br /><br />You can find this review and more on my blog <a href="http://www.missprint.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Miss Print</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13213967003546932204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1069682260?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780688096861" href="/book/show/607704.Castle_in_the_Air">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=library-has">library-has</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1069682260" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3390067964344739004">In this sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294.Howl_s_Moving_Castle__Howl_s_Moving_Castle___1_' title='Howl's Moving Castle (Howl's Moving Castle, #1) by Diana Wynne Jones' rel='nofollow noopener'>Howl's Moving Castle</a>, the wizard Howl gets mixed up with djinni, genies (in this story they're two different species) and some Arabian Nights-type characters (from the sanitized version I read as a child). Abdullah, a humble young carpet merchant with big (day)dreams, is sold a magic carpet by a suspicious-looking stranger, which leads him to a beautiful princess named Flower-in-the-Night, a genie in a bottle, and other adventures. Abdullah is forced to leave behind his daydrea</span>
  <span id="freeText3390067964344739004" style="display:none">In this sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294.Howl_s_Moving_Castle__Howl_s_Moving_Castle___1_" title="Howl's Moving Castle (Howl's Moving Castle, #1) by Diana Wynne Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">Howl's Moving Castle</a>, the wizard Howl gets mixed up with djinni, genies (in this story they're two different species) and some Arabian Nights-type characters (from the sanitized version I read as a child). Abdullah, a humble young carpet merchant with big (day)dreams, is sold a magic carpet by a suspicious-looking stranger, which leads him to a beautiful princess named Flower-in-the-Night, a genie in a bottle, and other adventures. Abdullah is forced to leave behind his daydreams and take action when a djinn kidnaps Flower and takes her to his castle in the air to be one of his many wives. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414509103i/11661238._SX540_.png" width="295" height="198" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Eventually Abdullah's and Flower's story twines together with some of the main characters from <i>Howl's Moving Castle</i>.<br><br>Abdullah's ability to use flowery language to good effect is told with affectionate humor:<blockquote>"O elegant tapestry of enchantment," Abdullah said, "O carpet composed of most complex cantrips, I pray you to move at a sedate speed toward Kingsbury, but to exercise the great wisdom woven in your fabric to make sure that we are not seen by anyone on the way."<br><br>Obediently the carpet climbed through the mist. . . A hoarse and trembling voice said from the bottle, "Do you have to flatter it so disgustingly?"<br><br>"This carpet," said Abdullah, "unlike you, is of an ensorcellment so pure and excellent that it will listen only to the finest of language. It is at heart a poet among carpets."<br><br>A certain smugness spread through the pile of the carpet. It held its tattered edges proudly straight and sailed sweetly forward into the golden sunlight above the mist.</blockquote>This was a fun, delightful Aladdin type of story, great for middle grade/YA ages and anyone who enjoys children's lit. The plot is a little smoother and easier to follow than <i>Howl's Moving Castle</i>, but perhaps also a little less engaging and complex. If you've read that book, the ending of this one will be more enjoyable and make more sense, but I think it could still be enjoyed without having read <i>Howl</i> first.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2069687789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18357736572436670033">I feel rather conned here. This story was not the experience I was expecting, especially when Howl's moving castle is one of my favourite stories. The only worthy part of this particular book, is the cover. It's attractive and inviting but the plot, not so much.<br/><br/>I love Howl's moving castle, as it was beautiful, exciting, and the characters were different. In this installment, the main character was irritating as hell. He just wasn't likeable, and in my opinion, this was entirely due to the writin</span>
  <span id="freeText18357736572436670033" style="display:none">I feel rather conned here. This story was not the experience I was expecting, especially when Howl's moving castle is one of my favourite stories. The only worthy part of this particular book, is the cover. It's attractive and inviting but the plot, not so much.<br /><br />I love Howl's moving castle, as it was beautiful, exciting, and the characters were different. In this installment, the main character was irritating as hell. He just wasn't likeable, and in my opinion, this was entirely due to the writing style of the author.<br /><br />It came to my attention, that Abdullah (our main character) was thinking about a woman (Flower-in-the-night) and described her as being educated, but also as beautiful and thin. So, in order for a woman to be beautiful, she just HAS to be referred to as thin, too? This has been happening as long as time, and it's damaging, as well as tiring. <br /><br />The main cast from the previous book are in this, but definitely not enough, and Abdullah alone is not enough to make a story entertaining and whimsical. So disappointed with this, and I'm unsure whether I will go on to finish this series. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1325601064" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1325601064" />
    <a title="Cat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42640402-cat"><img alt="Cat" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430360168p2/42640402.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1325601064?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cat" href="/user/show/42640402-cat">Cat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1325601064&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1325601064" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16637052351501056858">Going back to reread one of favourite childhood authors has opened my eyes to some of the problematic aspects of Jones' writing. <br/><br/>First of all, I tried to understand the story through Abdullah's narration. There is a possibility that he was not a reliable narrator, so Flower-in-the-Night's beauty could have been greatly exaggerated. Still, every chance he gets, he describes her astounding beauty--oh, and she's also clever to boot, so that's a bonus, but definitely not needed. It irritated me that</span>
  <span id="freeText16637052351501056858" style="display:none">Going back to reread one of favourite childhood authors has opened my eyes to some of the problematic aspects of Jones' writing. <br /><br />First of all, I tried to understand the story through Abdullah's narration. There is a possibility that he was not a reliable narrator, so Flower-in-the-Night's beauty could have been greatly exaggerated. Still, every chance he gets, he describes her astounding beauty--oh, and she's also clever to boot, so that's a bonus, but definitely not needed. It irritated me that they could fall in love so quickly--they knew each other for less than three days before they were married in a double wedding--under false pretenses. Abdullah only loved Flower for her beauty; Flower only loved Abdullah because he was the first man besides her father with whom she had made contact. Both of them were incredibly naive, having had no chance to get to know each other before they were married. When Flower was acting coldly towards Abdullah, I thought, "Great, the other princesses have educated her about her plans for a hasty elopement. Now she knows that Abdullah only valued her for her beauty and, while it was nice of him to come to her rescue, she certainly didn't need him." But, what happens instead? She acts all haughty because he didn't kiss her. Of all the things to get mad at him for--this scene was truly a giant face-palm. <br /><br />Speaking of hasty marriages, what was that scene between the soldier/Prince Justin and Princess Beatrice? He only chose her because she was one of the least attractive people in the room and she "looked like she could mend his clothes"? Who agrees to this kind of marriage proposal? Oh, Princess Beatrice of course. Again, two characters who do not know each other at all somehow end up together because the woman is naive enough to comply. <br /><br />I guess what I'm working towards is that the females in this world are so weakly written that they become part of the landscape rather than characters themselves. The women do nothing but clean (Sophie in the first book), cook (Martha), sew (Princess Beatrice), and have babies (almost all of the Hatters immediately after the events of Howl's Moving Castle). While there's nothing wrong to choose these lives for themselves, I felt it a great injustice to have their heroism taken away by men with magic. Sophie, a great magician herself, must rely on the Wizard Sulliman, Howl, Abdullah, the soldier, etc. to save her. Clever and logical Flower had to wait around for Abdullah to rescue her. Even Lettie, Sophie's strong-willed sister, was made to kept her powers secret because "Ben doesn't like people to know that I can do magic". The only thing worse than their constantly getting overshadowed is the fact that the men view nothing wrong with this. Abdullah doesn't like Sophie for being strong-willed. He views this trait--as well as other traits like being fat--to be undesirable in women. And, of course, he is right, for the two "fat, ugly girls" that he was nearly "forced" into marrying are vain and stupid--just as he predicted--and have no problem spending the rest of eternity in exile with an immature and spoiled djinn. Great. What an strong message for young girls who read this story. <br /><br />While I certainly haven't lost my awe for Jones' vivid imagery and her descriptive writing of these far-off magical kingdoms, it seems that I have lost respect for her characters. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16637052351501056858" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2541687913" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2541687913" />
    <a title="Fran" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/74816651-fran"><img alt="Fran" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586773357p2/74816651.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fran" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fran" href="/user/show/74816651-fran">Fran</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/74816651-fran?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2541687913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13086528023738066234">Let's start with the important part. I did like this book. A lot. Now, if you don't like authors who play with our preconceive ideas of how stories and characters should work, you won't like this book as much as I did. Because that's how Wynne Jones build her stories, by playing with the understood to make it new.<br/><br/>No, to matter at hand, my review: Castle in the Air is a companion book to Howl’s Moving Castle. It's the story of Abdullah, a young merchant from Zanzib. One day, a mysterious man sell</span>
  <span id="freeText13086528023738066234" style="display:none">Let's start with the important part. I did like this book. A lot. Now, if you don't like authors who play with our preconceive ideas of how stories and characters should work, you won't like this book as much as I did. Because that's how Wynne Jones build her stories, by playing with the understood to make it new.<br /><br />No, to matter at hand, my review: Castle in the Air is a companion book to Howl’s Moving Castle. It's the story of Abdullah, a young merchant from Zanzib. One day, a mysterious man sells him a magic carpet. The carpet, one of those inanimate objects that nonetheless seems to have a mind of its own, leads him into a lovely garden where he meets and falls in love with Princess Flower-in-the-Night, only to have her snatched by a djinn. Abdullah, then, sets off to rescue his love with the help of his magic carpet and the good head on his shoulders.<br /><br />Like in Howl's Moving castle, in this second book, Winne Jones impresses me by weaving together a story from what it seems are a series of random details, which significance only becomes evident as the plot advances. In this novel nothing is wasted, for every word, every scene, every character has is place and reason to be. Some help us see this new and unknown world while others give substance to the story.<br /><br />Wynne Jones plays with out expectations, giving us insta-love that while seemingly cliche in fact is there to show that falling in love is rather an excuse and not a reason to change our lives and go for an adventure. <br /><br />A truly enjoyable read.<br /> <br /> </span>

<div id="review_1364793693" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1364793693" />
    <a title="Amber" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46002774-amber"><img alt="Amber" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562115454p2/46002774.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1364793693?book_show_action=true">Jun 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber" href="/user/show/46002774-amber">Amber</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061478772" href="/book/show/2294535.Castle_in_the_Air">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46002774-amber?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1364793693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8144754737100469997">2.5 ⭐️<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1561939038ra/27748617.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>O.K I was super disappointed by this one. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16204601.Howl_s_Moving_Castle__Howl_s_Moving_Castle___1_' title='Howl's Moving Castle (Howl's Moving Castle, #1) by Diana Wynne Jones' rel='nofollow noopener'>Howl's Moving Castle</a> is one of my all time favorite books. I wasn't expecting this to be my next favorite, but I was hoping for the same whimsy and charm. Instead I got this story that mad me mad, because I hated the main character. I hated him because of the writing, which seems to be a product of it's time. But I will list some of my most hated passages that describe our MC's thoughts. <br/><br/><blockquote> "She (the Flower in the Night/ Love interest) was intelligen</blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText8144754737100469997" style="display:none">2.5 ⭐️<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1561939038ra/27748617.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>O.K I was super disappointed by this one. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16204601.Howl_s_Moving_Castle__Howl_s_Moving_Castle___1_" title="Howl's Moving Castle (Howl's Moving Castle, #1) by Diana Wynne Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">Howl's Moving Castle</a> is one of my all time favorite books. I wasn't expecting this to be my next favorite, but I was hoping for the same whimsy and charm. Instead I got this story that mad me mad, because I hated the main character. I hated him because of the writing, which seems to be a product of it's time. But I will list some of my most hated passages that describe our MC's thoughts. <br><br><blockquote> "She (the Flower in the Night/ Love interest) was intelligent, educated, and kind as well as being beautiful (and thin). pg 70"</blockquote><br><br><b>Seriously? How harmful is that?</b><br><br><blockquote>"In Zanzib everyone hated cats. People thought of them as very little better than the rats and mice they ate. If a cat came near you, you kicked it, and you drowned any kittens you could lay hands on. pg 172" </blockquote><br><br><b>I think I was mostly just shocked by this. It's not like I think books should only praise cats, but I wasn't expecting drowning kittens when I was going into this. </b><br><br><blockquote>"If he compared Flower-in-the-Night with Sophie, who had displeased him for being so strong-minded, he knew Flower-in-the-Night had twice Sophie's strength of mind. And as far as Abdullah was concerned, this only made Flower-in-the-Night more excellent. pg 318" </blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1561939038ra/27748618.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Nobody talks about Sophie like that. AND you shouldn't compare women, or even consider "strong-mindedness" a bad thing! Again how harmful is that?</b><br><br>So yeah, Abdullah could be freaking sexist jerk sometimes. The only redeeming quality of this novel was the last 20 pages because Calcifer makes me laugh my ass off and I love him. I plan on reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2173611.House_of_Many_Ways__Howl_s_Moving_Castle___3_" title="House of Many Ways (Howl's Moving Castle, #3) by Diana Wynne Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">House of Many Ways</a> and I am hoping that it doesn't disappoint me. I liked the story for the most part thus the 2.5 rating. It had a familiar whimsy but what made the first book so good was the characters and the characters in here aren’t great. The main cast may be in this but it’s complicated.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8144754737100469997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68925079" />
    <a title="Krystle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle"><img alt="Krystle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403921272p2/2639204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/68925079?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krystle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krystle" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle">Krystle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68925079" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3029106405169193899">Castle in the Air is the sequel to Howl’s Moving Castle. That being said I picked this up with trepidation because I was rather disappointed the book wasn’t going to be from the main characters in the first, nor would it have a direct focus on it. But they do occur later on.<br/><br/>That being said, I loved this book! I loved how she managed to turn this into another one of her witty, light-hearted, but not lacking in depth, fantasy tales. It was unique, original, and if I hadn’t read spoilers beforehand</span>
  <span id="freeText3029106405169193899" style="display:none">Castle in the Air is the sequel to Howl’s Moving Castle. That being said I picked this up with trepidation because I was rather disappointed the book wasn’t going to be from the main characters in the first, nor would it have a direct focus on it. But they do occur later on.<br /><br />That being said, I loved this book! I loved how she managed to turn this into another one of her witty, light-hearted, but not lacking in depth, fantasy tales. It was unique, original, and if I hadn’t read spoilers beforehand I would have been quite shocked at the twist at the end. It was quite ingenious how she managed to trick us throughout the whole book. Her descriptions and writing were fabulous as always, and she never manages to fall into the cliché. <br /><br /> <br />Definitely a wonderful book. Even if the summary doesn’t sound as engaging as the first novel, give it a chance because it’s an excellent read that will more than satisfy you at the end.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3029106405169193899" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/36306002-katerina-kondrenko?shelf=plot-driven-by-action">plot-driven-by-action</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1381902916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1360033420319757816"><b>
  <blockquote>8.5 out of 10</blockquote>
</b><br/><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog<br/><a href='http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/10/castle-in-air-by-diana-wynne-jones.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br/><br/><b>Short-Soundtrack:</b><br/><a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bACjyJAhEqc' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>John Me – Love Is My Drug, Is My Medicine</a><br/><br/><b>Genre</b>: fairytale, fantasy<br/><b>Stuff</b>: jinn, flying carpet and castle, magic<br/><b>Fail: </b>funny, but not charismatic MC<br/><b>WOW</b>: old characters, the plot, humor<br/><b>POV</b>: 3rd person, male<br/><b>Love-Geometry</b>: none<br/><br/><b>Quote-Core</b>: <blockquote>
  <i>“Fate doesn't care most of the t</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText1360033420319757816" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>8.5 out of 10</blockquote>
</b><br><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog<br><a href="http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/10/castle-in-air-by-diana-wynne-jones.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br><br><b>Short-Soundtrack:</b><br><a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=bACjyJAhEqc" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">John Me – Love Is My Drug, Is My Medicine</a><br><br><b>Genre</b>: fairytale, fantasy<br><b>Stuff</b>: jinn, flying carpet and castle, magic<br><b>Fail: </b>funny, but not charismatic MC<br><b>WOW</b>: old characters, the plot, humor<br><b>POV</b>: 3rd person, male<br><b>Love-Geometry</b>: none<br><br><b>Quote-Core</b>: <blockquote>
  <i>“Fate doesn't care most of the time.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Okay, I have to admit, I pick this book up thinking only about Howl and ended up being indifferent in new characters' fates, but the story itself and the writing (especially Russian translation) were super funny and smart, plus old heroes had played their roles, so overall I'm happy and ready for more.<br><br>This installment's adventures start in <b>Zanzib</b> where we meet <b>Abdullah</b> who sells carpets and loves to dream. One day a stranger offers him an old magical item which soon changes the boy's life: he falls in love, but his sweetheart gets abducted and Abdullah has to save not only her, but his own life too. Danger is everywhere, but with a flying carpet, a nasty jinn, a skillful solder and a few crazy cats the boy will go to <b>Ingary</b> and become a hero.<br><br>In this part we'll see Howl and Sophie, Lettie and her husband (until this book I wasn't sure whom she will marry: prince or mage), little Valeria, Calcifer and others. It's been only a year since the ending of the book #1, but there are serious news about everyone. <b>Howl and Sophie</b> now one of my favorite pairings. They aren't your typical HEA-couple, their quarrel, they fight, they know each other's flaws and don't mind them at all, 'cause you can't love a person partially, only whole. I'd love to see these two in a more mature setting, it might be firework-ish!<br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://3.bp.blogspot.com/-CbuYXzN7v74/WBWeJx4vLJI/AAAAAAAABLM/3HZY4yCwBXIL6c8mV_V6RJU_ylPo2yBswCLcB/s1600/142b7deebb2c.jpeg" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="314" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1477812902i/20996433.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div>(c) <a href="http://taka0801.deviantart.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">taka0801</a><br><br>Again, I wanna praise the <b>plot</b>. So many different lines interlace and turn into a well-thought-out and logical netting. Silly and naive moments open up from another side, as well as characters' natures and motivations. And after you've done with the book you wanna re-read it again, 'cause so many things will be different now when you know every secret and twist. That's magic!<br><br><b>
  <i>Diana Wynne Jones</i>
</b> knows how to surprise and entertain her readers during their read. I wasn't bored even once. I also need to highlight Jones's wits and humor (and many thanks to the Russian translator who did GREAT). I might not be in love with the new narrator, but I did enjoy his way of thoughts and speech. <br><br>I can't say more, 'cause this book is too intricate not to give a spoiler away by touching its threads. So I just let a content sigh out and run for the book #3.<br><br><b>Howl's Moving Castle (Ходячий замок):</b><br><blockquote>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1381902730" rel="nofollow noopener">Howl's Moving Castle</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1791065046" rel="nofollow noopener">(Ходячий замок)</a> #1/3<br>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1381902916" rel="nofollow noopener">Castle in the Air (Воздушный замок)</a> #2/3<br>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1381902945" rel="nofollow noopener">House of Many Ways (Дом с характером)</a> #3/3</blockquote></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1053109579" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9244451188891950654">This is one of DWJ's more problematic stories. Although very readable and amusing, it dips into uncomfortable territory with its portrayal of a middle east culture, and there are multiple instances of using fat as a characterisation of bad, lazy or shallow.<br/><br/>I think most problematic for me, however, is the plain princess who is so complimented to be chosen over more beautiful princesses that she's _grateful_ to be blackmailed into marriage.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_183253325" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/183253325" />
    <a title="Erin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3947264-erin"><img alt="Erin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389401312p2/3947264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/183253325?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/3947264-erin">Erin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780688096861" href="/book/show/607704.Castle_in_the_Air">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=brings-the-lolz">brings-the-lolz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=great-characters">great-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=little-romance">little-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=childrens-book">childrens-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=plot-twist">plot-twist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=love-the-protag">love-the-protag</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947264-erin?shelf=poc-protag">poc-protag</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer183253325" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5150053113986715124">If you read and enjoyed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294.Howl_s_Moving_Castle__Castle___1_' title='Howl's Moving Castle (Castle, #1) by Diana Wynne Jones' rel='nofollow noopener'>Howl's Moving Castle</a> and have yet to read this, what are you waiting for? Come on now, go read it. At once.<br/><br/>I liked <i>Castle in the Air</i> better than its predecessor, surprisingly. There are several reasons for this:<br/><br/>1. The plot makes more sense on a first read-- there's a clear mission from the get-go, and the reveals at the end aren't at all confusing.<br/><br/>2. It's not exactly a retelling... but there are clear, surely intended parallels to the story of Aladdin. I really liked the </span>
  <span id="freeText5150053113986715124" style="display:none">If you read and enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294.Howl_s_Moving_Castle__Castle___1_" title="Howl's Moving Castle (Castle, #1) by Diana Wynne Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">Howl's Moving Castle</a> and have yet to read this, what are you waiting for? Come on now, go read it. At once.<br /><br />I liked <i>Castle in the Air</i> better than its predecessor, surprisingly. There are several reasons for this:<br /><br />1. The plot makes more sense on a first read-- there's a clear mission from the get-go, and the reveals at the end aren't at all confusing.<br /><br />2. It's not exactly a retelling... but there are clear, surely intended parallels to the story of Aladdin. I really liked the setting, which was a fantasy version of Arabia.<br /><br />3. The biggest plus factor of all was the protagonist, Abdullah. <b>Oh, ABDULLAH!</b> He was the icing on the cake, the apple of my eye, etc etc. I feel both giddy and lucky to have read this book and it was an honor to experience 199 pages of pure Abdullah goodness. To know Abdullah is to love him. I adored his way of speaking, the manners of his psuedo-Arabian upbringing which led to delightful passages like:<br /><br /><i>"O most excellent of carpets," he said, "O brightest-colored and most delicately woven, whose lovely textile is so cunningly enhanced with magic, I fear I have not treated you hitherto with proper respect. I have snapped commands and even shouted at you, where I now see that your gentle nature requires only the mildest of requests. Forgive, oh, forgive!"</i><br /><br />Oh, yeah, that's right. In case the Aladdin thing didn't clue you in, there is a MAGIC CARPET. And a GENIE. If this doesn't appeal to you, I can't even begin to understand your strange, strange mind. MAGIC CARPET! GENIE! <br /><br /><i>Castle in the Air</i> might confuse some readers at first-- if you go in expecting another book full of Sophie, Howl, and Calcifer, you're in for a surprise. They don't come into the narrative until close to the very end. But Abdullah more than makes up for their absence, don't fret! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[On that note, I seriously loved the twist that those three were actually there the whole time. My only complaint: where's Michael? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />It's hard to think of anything negative to say about this one. There were a couple typos? I guess the reason it didn't get five stars from me is that 1. I'm stubbornly miserly in giving away my precious, precious stars, and 2. Even though I enjoyed every second of it (Every. Single. Second.), the writing style was a tad detached, so I didn't quite get the emotional depth that I require for five stars.<br /><br />I will most definitely be purchasing this book at some point. Highly recommended! </span>
  <a data-text-id="5150053113986715124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_48920722" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/48920722" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1394928-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405367803p2/1394928.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/48920722?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/1394928-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=audio-avail-ill">audio-avail-ill</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=pulitzerandrunnersupandmore">pulitzerandrunnersupandmore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=friend-love">friend-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=ill-request">ill-request</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1394928-laura?shelf=interlibloan">interlibloan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48920722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12857176357534722217">What a great follow up to the first in the series, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294.Howl_s_Moving_Castle__Howl_s_Moving_Castle___1_' title='Howl's Moving Castle (Howl's Moving Castle, #1) by Diana Wynne Jones' rel='nofollow noopener'>Howl's Moving Castle</a>! <br/><br/>This isn't a typical series in that the main characters from the first book don't appear in the second book until about 2/3 of the way through. But the humor and the whimsical magic and great characters are still very much here. I also enjoy the way animals play a significant role in her stories. They make the most interesting characters!<br/><br/>I'm thoroughly enjoying becoming reacquainted with DWJ. She has written so many books, </span>
  <span id="freeText12857176357534722217" style="display:none">What a great follow up to the first in the series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294.Howl_s_Moving_Castle__Howl_s_Moving_Castle___1_" title="Howl's Moving Castle (Howl's Moving Castle, #1) by Diana Wynne Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">Howl's Moving Castle</a>! <br /><br />This isn't a typical series in that the main characters from the first book don't appear in the second book until about 2/3 of the way through. But the humor and the whimsical magic and great characters are still very much here. I also enjoy the way animals play a significant role in her stories. They make the most interesting characters!<br /><br />I'm thoroughly enjoying becoming reacquainted with DWJ. She has written so many books, and I'm grateful for that. Her humor and effortlessly created magical worlds make me feel like a little kid again as I read, and Jenny Sterlin does a magnificent job with the narration of this entire series. <br /><br />2020 just may be a DWJ year for me. No one does humor and magic the way she does. This seems to be my sweet reading spot right now. 💚</span>
  <a data-text-id="12857176357534722217" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7242376840494088287">I turned out to enjoy this one a good deal better than I did Howl's Moving Castle. Perhaps it's got something to do with how I tend to prefer the Arabian Nights setting for my fairytales. But most of it, I think, is because the story was a great deal more straightforward and easier to follow, a simple Hero's Journey rather than a magical mystery whose rules we only vaguely know of, with characters that I could sympathize with better because their desires and needs were much less complex.<br/><br/>So with </span>
  <span id="freeText7242376840494088287" style="display:none">I turned out to enjoy this one a good deal better than I did Howl's Moving Castle. Perhaps it's got something to do with how I tend to prefer the Arabian Nights setting for my fairytales. But most of it, I think, is because the story was a great deal more straightforward and easier to follow, a simple Hero's Journey rather than a magical mystery whose rules we only vaguely know of, with characters that I could sympathize with better because their desires and needs were much less complex.<br /><br />So with a number of complaints suddenly removed, I could just enjoy the merits of Diana Wynne Jones to their fullest. Very nice.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sesana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sesana" href="/user/show/5172893-sesana">Sesana</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780688096861" href="/book/show/607704.Castle_in_the_Air">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5172893-sesana?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer156585665" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13346167098812287232">Castle in the Air is indeed a companion to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294.Howl_s_Moving_Castle__Castle___1_' title='Howl's Moving Castle (Castle, #1) by Diana Wynne Jones' rel='nofollow noopener'>Howl's Moving Castle</a>, but the first thing to accept is that you won't be seeing much of Howl and Sophie. Once I did that, I was able to relax and enjoy this entirely different book.<br/><br/>Abdullah is from Rashpuht, and this is where the story begins. As the names suggest, there's a definite "Arabian Nights" flavor to the narrative. Abdullah finds himself with a magic carpet, that he doesn't know how to control, exactly, and meets with the princess Flowers-in-t</span>
  <span id="freeText13346167098812287232" style="display:none">Castle in the Air is indeed a companion to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6294.Howl_s_Moving_Castle__Castle___1_" title="Howl's Moving Castle (Castle, #1) by Diana Wynne Jones" rel="nofollow noopener">Howl's Moving Castle</a>, but the first thing to accept is that you won't be seeing much of Howl and Sophie. Once I did that, I was able to relax and enjoy this entirely different book.<br /><br />Abdullah is from Rashpuht, and this is where the story begins. As the names suggest, there's a definite "Arabian Nights" flavor to the narrative. Abdullah finds himself with a magic carpet, that he doesn't know how to control, exactly, and meets with the princess Flowers-in-the-Night. Who is kidnapped right in front of him by an evil djinn. And so Abdullah goes on a quest to rescue his beloved, which eventually brings him to Ingary, and into contact with characters from the previous book.<br /><br />There's some really fantastic characters in here. Abdullah himself, who is a smooth talker but quite sincere in his love for Flowers-in-the-Night. Flowers-in-the-Night herself, who isn't content to be in distress and who is as intelligent as she is beautiful. And Princess Beatrice in particular, though she isn't in much of the book.<br /><br />The plot has a traditional fairy tale feel to it, with some twists. It also has the same sort of chaotic ending that Howl's Moving Castle had, which I liked. I'm very eager to continue the series now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13346167098812287232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4803729699493351519">I thought this was really fun read, just slightly more than Howl's Moving Castle, which I was surprised by! The main character in this one, Abdullah, speaks in the most ridiculous, flowery way, and I loved it! I can see why people might get bored of it after a while, but I continued to find it very charming.   <span id="freeText4803729699493351519" style="display:none">I thought this was really fun read, just slightly more than Howl's Moving Castle, which I was surprised by! The main character in this one, Abdullah, speaks in the most ridiculous, flowery way, and I loved it! I can see why people might get bored of it after a while, but I continued to find it very charming. Probably my main issue was Abdullah equating slimness with beauty, and of course the whole insta-love thing between him and Flower-in-the-Night (what a name...). I was so intrigued to find out how exactly this is a sequel to Howl's Moving Castle though, and I really liked how that was revealed! <br /><br />Overall I found this a delightfully cute read and I'd say it's a 3.5-4 star from me.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_353409735" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/353409735" />
    <a title="Heidi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5812324-heidi"><img alt="Heidi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489091071p2/5812324.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/353409735?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heidi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heidi" href="/user/show/5812324-heidi">Heidi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780061478772" href="/book/show/2294535.Castle_in_the_Air">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer353409735" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5188246125772469569">One of the marks of my favorite authors is their ability to keep me guessing–the knowledge that when I crack open one of their books, I should expect the unexpected. This is only my second Diana Wynne Jones read, but I can already see her name rising in the ranks of the authors who do just that. Like Howl’s Moving Castle, Castle in the Air is an incredibly smart, adventurous, twisting read that is a credit to readers of all ages. At no point did I know where the story was going, and in the end I</span>
  <span id="freeText5188246125772469569" style="display:none">One of the marks of my favorite authors is their ability to keep me guessing–the knowledge that when I crack open one of their books, I should expect the unexpected. This is only my second Diana Wynne Jones read, but I can already see her name rising in the ranks of the authors who do just that. Like Howl’s Moving Castle, Castle in the Air is an incredibly smart, adventurous, twisting read that is a credit to readers of all ages. At no point did I know where the story was going, and in the end I was so incredibly happy to see how it all ironed out, I can hardly wait to see some of my favorite characters back in House of Many Ways!<br /><br />Now, all of those twists and turns have a major drawback in the reviewing front in that it’s difficult to talk about a lot of the story in Castle in the Air without spoiling some things, so I’m going to be careful and brief! Abdullah as a main character provides an interested change of pace. Not only do we shift to the male point of view, but we also have a massive cultural shift in Castle in the Air. Somewhat of a more respectable Aladdin character, Abdullah is a hard-working, respectful carpet merchant rather bored with his current state of existence. Well, you know what they say, “May your life be interesting” is as much a curse as it is a blessing, and Abdullah’s life certainly takes a turn for the interesting in these pages. His cultural upbringing, far from the headstrong hills of Ingary, dictates that he speak in the most flattering and luminescent terms possible, also makes him a little unused to strong minded women (of which Castle in the Air has no shortage), and an expert at placating argumentative companions.<br /><br />Harnessed with a persnickety magic carpet, a somewhat vile genie, a soldier who looks trustworthy while awake, and most devious while sleeping, and a pair of most unusual cats, Abdullah is bent on rescuing his love and fulfilling the prophecies that were made at their births.<br /><br />While I did greatly enjoy Castle in the Air, I’m sad to say that my enjoyment did not come near that which I had for Howl’s Moving Castle. I appreciated that Abdullah was a completely different character from those we dealt with previously, but still what I loved so much about the first book were the characters Howl, Sophie, and Calcifer. For some reason, I’ve also never enjoyed the Arabian folklore as much, and I was somewhat confused by the presence of both a genie and djinn in this book. It was always my understanding that the word ‘genie’ was the American vernacular of the term ‘djinn’, but it would seem that in Castle in the Air they have completely different identities and mythologies entirely! The genie is a creature tied to a bottle that is required to grant wishes to their master–very similar to the popularized notions we’re accustomed to from pop culture like Disney’s Aladdin or the old TV series I Dream of Jeannie. The djinn, however, are more powerful beings that have no such ties, and from what I have read seem much closer to the creatures in Arabian mythology. If anyone has any more info/has read any good explanation of this, please let me know!<br /><br />Also, Ana of The Booksmugglers pointed out in a recent review Diana Wynne Jones’ perchance for writing very negatively of fat people. You know the glass shattering episode of How I Met Your Mother? Yep. I notice this now, and Castle in the Air was no exception, though I’m sure I would not have noticed it if it hadn’t been pointed out to me. We see this in the women Abdullah’s father’s first wive’s brother’s daughter Fatima (yep, you read that right) wants Abdullah to marry. Also, there was a point that made me uncomfortable where they slap a child to get her to stop crying, and recommend this sort of abusive behavior.<br /><br />Those quibbles aside, Castle in the Air is a wondrous adventure story which answers the question, what do you do when all of your dreams (and nightmares) come true? Fans of Howl’s Moving Castle will adore appearances by their favorite characters, and appreciate the wit, charm, and elegance that is Diana Wynne Jones’ writing. Oh, um…I said brief, right? Sorry…<br /><br />Originally reviewed at <a href="http://bunburyinthestacks.com/2012/07/20/retro-friday-review-castle-in-the-air-by-diana-wynne-jones/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bunbury in the Stacks</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5188246125772469569" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1143725580" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1143725580" />
    <a title="☆ ĄňŊǡƂėƮĦ ☆ ŞŧŎŋė" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34403359"><img alt="☆ ĄňŊǡƂėƮĦ ☆ ŞŧŎŋė" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1469758679p2/34403359.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

  <span id="freeText17553652908543254054" style="display:none"><br /><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />I feel bad for Castle in the Air because I love Howl's Moving Castle and I waited so long to get to it. I think this mostly seems lesser in comparison. And when it does start to really pick up, it's because the elements of book 1 show back up. It has that charm of a classic fairytale, for sure, but I just cared less about Abdullah and Flower in the Night. Flower improves by leaps and bounds when we spend a wee bit of time with her, but it wasn't nearly enough. There was so fat hate slipped in here, of the classic kind where the worst characters are also made fat, and every time it showed up I was taken out of the story. Overall, this was mostly sweet and generally good, but I don't foresee it becoming one I reread like I do Howl's. </span>

<div id="review_2518727169" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2518727169" />
    <a title="Emely Galindo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30718340-emely-galindo"><img alt="Emely Galindo" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2518727169?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emely Galindo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emely Galindo" href="/user/show/30718340-emely-galindo">Emely Galindo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2518727169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4051042110204341079">This book was NOTHING like Howl's Moving Castle. So much that I'm even doubting they have the same author. <br/>Howl's Moving Castle had well built, three-dimensional characters. Sophie, Howl, and Calcifer managed to have many flaws, and yet still be utterly likable.<br/>The characters in Castle in the Air were the complete opposite. Flower- in-the-night was just a pretty face, with no personality whatsoever.<br/>I mean at the end she proved to be resourceful for about 2 minutes, but then she still waits to be</span>
  <span id="freeText4051042110204341079" style="display:none">This book was NOTHING like Howl's Moving Castle. So much that I'm even doubting they have the same author. <br />Howl's Moving Castle had well built, three-dimensional characters. Sophie, Howl, and Calcifer managed to have many flaws, and yet still be utterly likable.<br />The characters in Castle in the Air were the complete opposite. Flower- in-the-night was just a pretty face, with no personality whatsoever.<br />I mean at the end she proved to be resourceful for about 2 minutes, but then she still waits to be rescued by Abdullah.<br />And Abullah was SO MUCH WORSE. He wassuch a hatable character. He hates animals, sees women like objects, and is so utterly shallow.<br />I don't even understand how you can write a character like that, after creating Howl.<br />And he is disgusted by his cousins just because they're not beautiful. What the fuck?<br />And it's not just that he didn't want to marry them. I mean, that's fine if you're not attracted to them.<br />But the fact that he didn't even consider they were PEOPLE with FEELINGS. Like damn, women don't have to pretty for you to see them as people.<br />It wasn't just shallowness, it was pure sexism.<br />Because Jamal, for example, wan't attractive, and yet Abdullah still saw him as a person and friend, and was kind to him.<br />But he can't see women as people? As friends?<br />It's like all they are to him is sexual objects.<br />But if we're talking about sexism, the whole SETTING was sexist.<br />An why would you write a book like that after HMC? Which was filled with strong, independent, badass women.<br />And an awesome fictional country.<br />WHY after that amazing setting, would you create a place (when you could create ANY place, ANY FUCKING PLACE IN THE ENTIRE WORLD) that is so disgustingly mysogynystic.<br />Like, we still live in a sexist world. But that world is 100x more sexist. And after Ingary was filled with so many admirable characters and women that children could look up to.<br />I'm don't even want to know how many little girls read this and thought that they had to pretty, so that they would be worth something. And that they would never be worth as much as a man. They could never be regarded as friends, or even people. All they were useful for was sexual pleasure and breeding. Oh, but don't forget cooking and cleaning and basically being a maid. <br />And obviousle, they couldn't be smart, or take leadership. That should be left to the men. And they couldn't be strong, or badass. That's impossible. They should wait for their husband, to complete them. And whatever problem they encountered, they should wait fro the more qualified man, to fix it and save them.<br />That is seriously the fucking message that little girls will get.<br />I don't even comprehend how someone can be so sexist, i mean i don't think i've ever read or seen anything as sexist as that. And a WOMAN wrote that? HOW?<br />I stand to reason that Dianna wasn't the author of this book. Instead, a man that wished to create a world in which women were worthless objects. Not freinds. Not smart. Less than people. THey had to be presentable for a man. Their whole goal in life is to marry. The man must be paid a dowry? To marry? And then being cooking cleaning maids, plus incubators, plus sex machines. <br />And of course, men can have as many as they want.<br />And they feel ENTITLED to women.<br />I mean honestly, they even ruined Justin.<br />I even liked him at the start. He loved animals, how could i not love him?<br />But then he wouldn't HELP fucking KIDNAPPED WOMEN, who would be married and presumably be forced to consumate the marriage and provide him sexual pleasure, at least, and bear children for him at most. So they would be raped not once, but endless times, for THE REST OF THEIR LIVES. They would be imprisoned there, away from their family and home.<br />Their whole lives taken away from them.<br />AND EVEN A FUCKING FOUR YEAR OLD. Imagine that, kidnapping and raping a four year old.<br />AND THIS IS A FUCKING CHILDREN'S BOOK.<br />So that fucking prince Justin says NO to saving sex trafficked women and a GIRL.<br />Unless he gets a princess, so he fucking will save the 3o girls from being married off to a stranger, but only if he gets ONE princess married of to a stranger, for himself.<br />What and ENTITLED ASS. So basically he wants one of the women to sell themselves in order to save the others. Basically having to leave her family, friends and home to leave with him and be his maid and sexual slave plus incubator.<br />But even if the setting and male characters weren't sexist. Even if the female characters weren't so useless and utterly submissive.<br />The romance, was non-existing. They knew each other for 2 nights and were already IN LOVE.<br />And Abdullah only liked her for her beauty, and Flower-in-the-night only like him because he was the FIRST MAN SHE HAD EVER SEEN.<br />What the fuck.<br />Not romantic AT ALL.<br />I mean i sort of liked the Middle Eastern setting, i it hadn't been so sexist. ANd i liked Justin, until he was sexist.<br />It's just honestly, the whole thing was so BLATANTLY sexist it fucking ruined the entire book.<br />I can overlook some minor sexism, but this was seriously THE MOST SEXIST BOOK I'VE EVER READ.<br />And that's saying something, because I've read so many books.<br />But honestly not even book, pure ANYTHING.<br />So yeah, it COULD have been a good book.<br />I don't know if it's because she was trying to write as what a Middle Eastern man thought like, and what a Middle Eastern country was like. But still, NO.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4051042110204341079" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
